  //<![CDATA[
    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }
    
    function initAppleId() {
      AppleID.auth.init({
        clientId : 'com.goodreads.app', 
        scope : 'name email',
        redirectURI: 'https://www.goodreads.com/apple_users/sign_in_with_apple_web',
        state: 'apple_oauth_state_8b5e9b33-82c5-4a54-8b38-dab4250b1c1f'
      });
    }
    
    var initializeSiwa = function() {
      var APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL =  "https://appleid.cdn-apple.com/appleauth/static/jsapi/appleid/1/en_US/appleid.auth.js"
      loadScript(APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL, initAppleId);
    };

      initAppleId();

      initializeSiwa();

<span id="freeTextContainer8142064350601535222"><i><b>Alona Dare</b>–Senior in high school, co-captain of the cheerleading squad, Homecoming Queen three years in a row, voted most likely to marry a movie star… and newly dead.</i><br/><br/>I’m the girl you hated in high school.   <span id="freeText8142064350601535222" style="display:none"><i><b>Alona Dare</b>–Senior in high school, co-captain of the cheerleading squad, Homecoming Queen three years in a row, voted most likely to marry a movie star… and newly dead.</i><br /><br />I’m the girl you hated in high school. Is it my fault I was born with it all-good looks, silky blond hair, a hot body, and a keen sense of what everyone else should not be wearing? But my life isn’t perfect, especially since I died. Run over by a bus of band geeks—is there anything more humiliating? As it turns out, yes—watching your boyfriend and friends move on with life, only days after your funeral. And you wouldn’t believe what they’re saying about me now that they think I can’t hear them. To top it off, I’m starting to disappear, flickering in and out of existence. I don’t know where I go when I’m gone, but it’s not good. Where is that freaking white light already?<br /><br /><i><b>Will Killian</b>–Senior in high school, outcast, dubbed “Will Kill” by the popular crowd for the unearthly aura around him, voted most likely to rob a bank…and a ghost-talker.</i><br /><br />I can see, hear, and touch the dead. Unfortunately, they can also see, hear and touch me. Yeah, because surviving high school isn’t hard enough already. I’ve done my best to hide my “gift.” After all, my dad, who shared my ability, killed himself because of it when I was fifteen. But lately, pretending to be normal has gotten a lot harder. A new ghost—an anonymous, seething cloud of negative energy with the capacity to throw me around—is pursuing me with a vengeance. My mom, who knows nothing about what I can do, is worrying about the increase in odd incidents, my shrink is tossing around terms like “temporary confinement for psychiatric evaluation,” and my principal, who thinks I’m a disruption and a faker, is searching for every way possible to get rid of me. How many weeks until graduation?</span>

<div class='communityQuestion'>
<div class='questionText'>
<a href="/questions/1022635-what-prompted-you-to-use-the-setting-you">What prompted you to use the setting you did? It was fun to read about familiar sites with a different name :)</a>
</div>
<div class='communityQAFooter questionFooter'>
<ul class='questionFooterActions'>
<li class='footerItem like'>
<span class='likeItContainer' id='like_container_community_question_1022635'><a id="like_count_community_question_1022635" rel="nofollow" href="/rating/voters/1022635?resource_type=CommunityQuestion"><span class="likesCount">1 like</span></a>&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;<a rel="nofollow" class="jsLike like_it" href="https://www.goodreads.com/user/new?remember=true&amp;return_url=%2Fbook%2Fshow%2F7008041-the-ghost-and-the-goth">like</a></span>

</li>
<li class='footerItem communityQuestionTimestamp'>
<a href="/questions/1022635-what-prompted-you-to-use-the-setting-you">3 years ago</a>
</li>

<div class='allCommunityAnswers'>
<div class='communityAnswer'>
<div class='communityAnswerBody'>
<div class='answererUserIcon'>
<a class="leftAlignedImage userPhoto" href="/user/show/2991722-stacey-kade"><img alt="" src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/users/1388764657i/2991722._UX100_CR0,25,100,100_.jpg" /></a>
</div>
<div class='communityAnswerTextContainer'>
<span class='communityAnswererName'>
<a href="/user/show/2991722-stacey-kade">Stacey Kade</a>
</span>
<span class='communityAnswerText'>
<span class="expandableContainer"><span class="truncatedContent">I wrote what I knew. :) Alona and Will's high school was my high school. Not haunted, though. At least as far as I know. But literally, the outfit she<a class="jsShow showAction" href="#">…more</a></span><span class="fullContent">I wrote what I knew. :) Alona and Will's high school was my high school. Not haunted, though. At least as far as I know. But literally, the outfit she's wearing on the cover--the white shirt and red short shorts? That was my high school gym outfit. :D <br /><br />I changed the names of towns and geography to suit my needs (and to protect the innocent...or guilty), but I lived in Mt. Zion, IL, which was a stand-in for Groundsboro. Both of them are just outside of Decatur. When someone talks about the smell of ADM and/or Staley's in the book, I know that smell because I lived there. <br /><br />Basically, it was my first time writing a YA novel, and I was nervous enough about writing characters who were so much younger that I wanted everything else to be something familiar. <br /><br />Fun story: When I wrote the first draft, waaaaay back in 2007, my sister read it for me as she was in high school at the time. At the end, she told me she really liked it but she wanted to know why no one was using cell phones. <br /><br />And it dawned on me--I'd left them out because no one was using cell phones like that (and smart phones didn't even exist) in 1993.<br /><br />So, every cell phone mention in the first book was added after the fact. <br /><br />All of that being said, none of the characters are based on real people. Though, I did borrow a certain last name from someone who wasn't the nicest to me in high school. ;)<a class="jsHide hideAction" href="#">(less)</a></span></span>
</span>
</div>
</div>

<div id="review_1825077855" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1825077855" />
    <a title="Cristina Monica" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/14596170-cristina-monica"><img alt="Cristina Monica" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1589617514p2/14596170.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1825077855?book_show_action=true">Nov 29, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Cristina Monica" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Cristina Monica" href="/user/show/14596170-cristina-monica">Cristina Monica</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="did not like it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">did not like it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14596170-cristina-monica?shelf=ghosts">ghosts</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1825077855" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer2902410722121041633">1.5 stars.<br/><br/>I feel like I’ve read this book a hundred times before.<br/><br/>Obviously, I haven’t, or I’d be mad right by now, but I couldn’t bring myself to find anything original about ‘‘The Ghost and the Goth’’ and I’m a huge fan of ghost books.<br/><br/>Tell me if this doesn’t sound familiar to you. A beautiful, popular blond cheerleader is hit by a bus and dies instantly. When she roams the hallways of her high school, she realizes that she wasn’t as loved as she thought.<br/><br/>It’s no surprise that this character in q</span>
  <span id="freeText2902410722121041633" style="display:none">1.5 stars.<br /><br />I feel like I’ve read this book a hundred times before.<br /><br />Obviously, I haven’t, or I’d be mad right by now, but I couldn’t bring myself to find anything original about ‘‘The Ghost and the Goth’’ and I’m a huge fan of ghost books.<br /><br />Tell me if this doesn’t sound familiar to you. A beautiful, popular blond cheerleader is hit by a bus and dies instantly. When she roams the hallways of her high school, she realizes that she wasn’t as loved as she thought.<br /><br />It’s no surprise that this character in question is extremely vain and self-centered. You must find her fun or funny to not be driven crazy by her constant whining. But she also has deeper problems—so it’s not like she is a complete Barbie.<br /><br />It’s just so, so, so predictable. But then again, I don’t think this is a book anyone would pick up to be surprised by tons of twists and turns. It’s also unrealistic—not that that’s a shock either—and very much feels that way. <br /><br />The idea of a ghost and a goth narrating this book sounded quite fun. But then the romance came in and—no, no, no. *eye roll* So expected, so predictable. And the goth just… he’s not sexy or at least a little swoon-worthy. Just another character. <br /><br />You know, it is just a feeling about my having read this book before, because now that I think about it, I’ve seen a lot of movies with a story similar to this one—‘‘Teen Spirit’’ is an example as well as all the ‘‘Christmas Carol’’ adaptations (see ‘‘Christmas Cupid’’!).<br /><br /><a href="https://hitormissbooks.wordpress.com/" rel="nofollow noopener">Blog</a> | <a href="https://www.youtube.com/c/LolaReviewer" rel="nofollow noopener">Youtube</a> | <a>Twitter</a> | <a>Instagram</a> | <a href="https://plus.google.com/u/0/105021852309973899120/posts" rel="nofollow noopener">Google+</a> | <a href="https://www.bloglovin.com/blogs/hit-miss-books-12564715" rel="nofollow noopener">Bloglovin’</a></span>
  <a data-text-id="2902410722121041633" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

    <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_1688645641" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1688645641" />
    <a title="Chelsea ❤Peril Please❤ " class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/8422853-chelsea-peril-please"><img alt="Chelsea ❤Peril Please❤ " src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1570038444p2/8422853.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1688645641?book_show_action=true">Jul 05, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Chelsea ❤Peril Please❤ " class="user" itemprop="url" name="Chelsea ❤Peril Please❤ " href="/user/show/8422853-chelsea-peril-please">Chelsea ❤Peril Please❤ </a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/8422853-chelsea-peril-please?shelf=favorites">favorites</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/8422853-chelsea-peril-please?shelf=alternating-pov">alternating-pov</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/8422853-chelsea-peril-please?shelf=could-read-over-and-over-again">could-read-over-and-over-again</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/8422853-chelsea-peril-please?shelf=unforgettable-male-leads">unforgettable-male-leads</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/8422853-chelsea-peril-please?shelf=don-t-be-fooled-by-the-cover">don-t-be-fooled-by-the-cover</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1688645641" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer7353915936369898585"><br/>There’s nothing better than a book that surprises you… in a good way. My story for this book is a long one, dating years back to when I added pretty much anything and everything to my ever-growing tbr pile. I was picky back then, too-Don’t be fooled. However, I didn’t quite know what I loved and how to decipher what made me tick, down to my deepest molecule. <br/><br/><a href='http://s1301.photobucket.com/user/ChelseaRoberts3/media/09d87715a98ba578102621d1c4f5ce493e261aa5c7bcd9f3b12bb55e992e24a9_zpstqxhndbg.jpg.html' target='_blank' rel='nofollow noopener'>
  <img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1468938356i/19761690._SX540_.jpg' alt=' photo 09d87715a98ba578102621d1c4f5ce493e261aa5c7bcd9f3b12bb55e992e24a9_zpstqxhndbg.jpg' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/>
</a><br/><br/>So when I did my most recent delete spree for my tbr pile, this had to go. I mean, it had all the signs of books I try to stay away fro</span>
  <span id="freeText7353915936369898585" style="display:none"><br>There’s nothing better than a book that surprises you… in a good way. My story for this book is a long one, dating years back to when I added pretty much anything and everything to my ever-growing tbr pile. I was picky back then, too-Don’t be fooled. However, I didn’t quite know what I loved and how to decipher what made me tick, down to my deepest molecule. <br><br><a href="http://s1301.photobucket.com/user/ChelseaRoberts3/media/09d87715a98ba578102621d1c4f5ce493e261aa5c7bcd9f3b12bb55e992e24a9_zpstqxhndbg.jpg.html" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1468938356i/19761690._SX540_.jpg" alt=" photo 09d87715a98ba578102621d1c4f5ce493e261aa5c7bcd9f3b12bb55e992e24a9_zpstqxhndbg.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><br>So when I did my most recent delete spree for my tbr pile, this had to go. I mean, it had all the signs of books I try to stay away from: Fugly cover (I know, I know, shut up), hardly any friend’s ratings, no quotes that appealed to me (but I'll change that in my review ;) ), and just nothing to back it up and not enough ratings. But, after reading my beloved Mediator series again, I was in the mood for this book. And guess what?? I immediately added it back onto my tbr and bought it immediately. Best decision I've ever made (well...).<br><br><b>
  <blockquote>I pulled the Dodge over to the side of the road on Henderson, next to the tennis courts, flipped the hazard lights on, and waited. Alona hadn’t committed suicide, I knew that. The girl had enough arrogance and self-esteem to choke a horse. She had, however, died a violent and unnatural death, which probably meant she was still tied to the exact place of her death.</blockquote>
</b><br><br>So, I guess since it's so late, I need to get right to the book, don't I? This story, while not wholly original (what story is these days, really), is done extremely well. That's just my opinion, but I think I read enough books to have a little bit of room to say that. I know what I like, I know what I don't, and <b>I'm actually quite picky</b>. This book, what with all its quirky humor and obvious disregard for what is now a social faux pas for our top reviewers today, <b>stood above all cliches</b>...by making itself into one.<br><br><b>
  <blockquote>I sighed. “Alona.” <br>“Good luck with class,” she said with faux cheer. “Hope you like musicals. I’ll make sure to tell them Annie is your favorite.” <br>“Wait, just wait a—” <br>Without another word, she slipped through the closed door, humming “Tomorrow” under her breath. <br>Great. Not only do I have an angry spirit guide, but an angry spirit guide with a vindictive streak and an unnatural knowledge of show tunes. Better and better already.</blockquote>
</b><br><br><a href="http://s1301.photobucket.com/user/ChelseaRoberts3/media/tumblr_minfd2YpXY1rgn9wro1_500_zpso1ngewwb.gif.html" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1468938356ra/19761691.gif" alt=" photo tumblr_minfd2YpXY1rgn9wro1_500_zpso1ngewwb.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><br>Now let me explain: Alona is your <b>typical stereotypical bitchy cheerleader</b>. So overdone, yeah? Well...that's all in who you ask. Me? I can appreciate a fun, over-the-top, cliched-and even cheesy-book if done correctly. Do you know how many times I desperately wish for more books like this that aren't trashed with horrid grammar, misspelling, and nasty characters you just can't root for? It's just unheard of these days, and I find it so comical that I turned my nose up to this one because, frankly, it was actually quite adorable. <br><br><b>
  <blockquote>“Good. I’m not goth.”<br>"Your hair is black, you have piercings, you wear black all the time and act all freaky—”<br>"My hair is naturally this color. I have three earrings in one ear, that’s it. This shirt”—I tugged at the fabric across my chest—“ is navy blue, and if I act weird all the time, it’s because of ghosts like you.”</blockquote>
</b><br><br><a href="http://s1301.photobucket.com/user/ChelseaRoberts3/media/download_zpsjbrmtkvg.jpg.html" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1468938442i/19761702.jpg" alt=" photo download_zpsjbrmtkvg.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><br>And that's the thing-it's all in your personality. For one, Will wasn't even a goth. I mean...perhaps he dresses a little dark, but he's hardly Emo. And his personality, another shocking factor, actually had me <b>swooning</b> from his first POV. He was actually...<b>butterfly inducing</b> from the moment I was in his head. Yikes. Shocked Chelsea. Chelsea is shocked.<br><br><b>
  <blockquote>"Are you staying … or just passing through?” I asked through gritted teeth. <br>“Why? Does it matter to you?” <br>A thousand smart-ass replies leaped to mind, but she would be expecting that. So, I went for the truth. “Yeah, it does.” <br>Her eyes widened and the faintest hint of pink spread across her face. I grinned. Had I just embarrassed Alona Dare, the Alona Dare?</blockquote>
</b><br><br>So back to my original point (man I can get off topic like no-one's business)-typical cheerleader. Judgmental. Rude. On a pedestal...but <b>she was <i>meant</i> to be</b> this way, therefore making her wholly likable (and don't forget what I said: Don't ever judge a book by its cover....)-She <b>had me laughing out loud</b> from chapter one on. Nothing felt overdone, nothing felt cheesy-it was all perfectly balanced and, frankly, had the sweetest message.<br><br><a href="http://s1301.photobucket.com/user/ChelseaRoberts3/media/tumblr_ngn9zjcoKt1u21hh4o1_500_zpsyhddbhfj.gif.html" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1468938356ra/19761692.gif" alt=" photo tumblr_ngn9zjcoKt1u21hh4o1_500_zpsyhddbhfj.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><br>But, hey, this obviously wasn't without its flaws or I'd have given five, right? I think a lot of my problem stemmed from <b>how fucking tired I was</b>. Endless tiredness. Endless running. Go Chelsea run Chelsea find Chelsea clean Chelsea-Go go go. So, yeah, putting this down every 10% really pissed me off, if I'm being honest. When you pick up a book fifty times in 100 different moods, it tends to effect a book. <br><br>And yes, while not wholly cheesy, it did have its more exaggerated moments-like his therapist-puh-<i>lease</i>. And Joonie-bleh. Also, I guess I wanted a little....more? But, candidly speaking, that's really all that bothered me. *shrugs* I just loved it so much.<br><br><b>
  <blockquote>“You don’t have to follow her,” I said. “It’s Friday. I know exactly where she’s going after school.” No way would Joonie miss a visit to Lily, not after what she’d told me today. <br>"So are we going, too, or what?” Alona idly flicked a piece of … ghost lint? … off her shorts.</blockquote>
</b><br><br>Refreshing, sweet, lots of banter between Will and Alona, and a story that actually fuels itself without reaching, I fell in love within moments. <b>Will was a beautifully tortured boy</b> that I totally didn't expect and Alona had a hidden life that no one could possibly see behind the veneer....just like she wanted. A story constructed of not only laughter and wise-ass remarks, but <b>learning what it means to be a kinder person</b>-even if she isn't with her kind anymore and even if she struggles with it up until the very end (perhaps more...). A book filled with <b>muddled social tiers</b> such as jocks and mean girls and cheating bfs, cliched to the max merely to make us laugh....and it surely succeeded. Whether this book is for you or not, I really don't know. But when life got just a little too tough around here, I turned to what makes me happy, and that's apparently a ghostly significant other, happy to haunt (and annoy) the one they love just because they can (a la Mediator :P). <br><br><i>For more of my reviews, please visit:</i><br><a href="http://starcrossedbookblog.com/chelsea-peril-please-reviews/" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1452287303i/17673713._SX540_.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><a title="Facebook" href="https://www.facebook.com/starcrossedbookblog" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1438055977i/15660595.png" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a> <a title="Twitter" href="https://twitter.com/starcrossedblog" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1438055639i/15660580.png" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a> <a title="RSS" href="http://feeds.feedburner.com/starcrossedbookblog/METU" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1438055639i/15660581.png" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a> <a title="BLOGLOVIN" href="https://www.bloglovin.com/blogs/star-crossed-book-blog-13035961" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1438055639i/15660579.png" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a> <a title="Google+" href="https://plus.google.com/u/0/b/116866754719786372049/+Starcrossedbookblog/posts" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1439651670i/15866819.png" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><br><br>************************<br><br>Well, <b>color me surprised</b>. This book was not at all what I perceived it to be, once again proving that you can't simply judge a book by its [horribly cheesy] cover. Cute, funny, witty, sarcastic, well-written, and not at all what I thought it would be like, I fell in love almost immediately with Alona's snarky attitude and Will's desperation to not see those who haven't went to their final resting place. <br><br>I still can't believe I loved this book as much as I did. Even more surprising is that I <u>can't wait</u> to read the second installment. For those of you judging this book by its cover...don't. It's way better than you would ever think-Even with it's stereotypical nature and play on the social tiers of High School (Though, I think this was done on purpose for comical intents and purposes) (which I loved, btw). <br><br>But, for those of you who need more convincing.....<br><br><b>RTC</b></span>
  <a data-text-id="7353915936369898585" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

  <div class="friendReviews elementListBrown" >
    <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_1544891977" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1544891977" />
    <a title="Michelle" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/8836060-michelle"><img alt="Michelle" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1487160141p2/8836060.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1544891977?book_show_action=true">Feb 11, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Michelle" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Michelle" href="/user/show/8836060-michelle">Michelle</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1544891977" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12602586917671104860">This was a pleasant and easy read! This screams YA, from the title to the cheesy cover. Actually, I was enticed by the cheesy cover, and the models looked exactly as how they were described in the book. The plot is simple but entertaining nonetheless. For this review though, I would like to focus on the heroine: Alona Dare. She's the main reason why I enjoyed reading this book. <br/><br/>I like reading YA but I've become more selective when it comes to this genre as I get older. Maybe it’s just my age, bu</span>
  <span id="freeText12602586917671104860" style="display:none">This was a pleasant and easy read! This screams YA, from the title to the cheesy cover. Actually, I was enticed by the cheesy cover, and the models looked exactly as how they were described in the book. The plot is simple but entertaining nonetheless. For this review though, I would like to focus on the heroine: Alona Dare. She's the main reason why I enjoyed reading this book. <br /><br />I like reading YA but I've become more selective when it comes to this genre as I get older. Maybe it’s just my age, but I’ve noticed an unnerving number of cookie cutter heroines. They are different from "other" girls within their own stories, but ironically just a dime a dozen in the YA genre. Besides this, I wonder why they imply that just because someone is different (she’s not into hair and makeup, she’d rather read a book, fight demons, etc.) she is somehow unable to relate to “normal” girls. Further, that “normal” girls will never understand her and she will always be ostracized or bullied by them unfairly. This classification of “normal” girls and “weird” girls can’t contain the diversity of young girls in this world, let alone a classroom.<br /><br />Alona Dare subverts this trope. Stacey Kade has created a character that is stereotypically an antagonist and instead made her the unabashed heroine. She is the epitome of a gorgeous queen bee and she doesn’t let other people make her feel bad for her actions or her thoughts unless she is truly at fault. Actually, the story itself doesn’t shy away from tearing Alona down, and she has to come to terms with the ugly truth of how her actions affected the people around her. Despite that, Alona doesn’t accept responsibility for the behavior of her friends or her enemies, and she doesn’t try to change herself so that people will like her more. She knows who she is, and she knows who she is isn’t wrong. When Alona admits her mistakes, she admits them as mistakes in actions, not in character.<br /><br />As queen bees go, Alona is pretty good at getting what she wants but her skill at manipulation isn't treated as villainous. Instead, they’re used to assist her love interest’s character development. Will Killian begins the novel as your stereotypical emo kid. Alona comes in, watches his struggles, and tells him, "We can fix this. We can make people see the real you, but first you have to understand how society functions. You have to play the game, and then things can go your way." Their dynamic reflects another subversion of the YA romantic trope: that the girl is an unwelcomed misfit, and the guy is a popular Adonis just waiting to find the right manic pixie dream girl to call his own. Instead, Alona is Will’s Aphrodite, and Will her manic pixie dream boy.<br /><br />What I'm trying to get at with this extensive review (and for such a light book, at that!), is that we need more characters like Alona. Teenage girls need to realize that the popular girl in their class is not their archenemy. She can be their friend. She can be their frenemy. She can be whatever they want her to be in their lives, or whatever she wants to be. Every girl can be whatever they want to be. Diversity is beautiful! Dang, I feel ancient...</span>
  <a data-text-id="12602586917671104860" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer1019373351666623959">I just finished this two minutes ago and I have THE BIGGEST grin on my face.<br/><br/>I don't know if I have a soft spot for ghosts (yeah, right) or for KICK-ASS characters,<br/>but luckyly for me, this book happens to have both.<br/><br/>So imagine how happy I was all through this read.<br/><br/>I randomly found the book description here in goodreads and was blown away by how<br/>similar it sounded to <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/187811.Shadowland__The_Mediator___1_' title='Shadowland (The Mediator, #1) by Meg Cabot' rel='nofollow noopener'>Shadowland</a> my all time favorite YA series.   <span id="freeText1019373351666623959" style="display:none">I just finished this two minutes ago and I have THE BIGGEST grin on my face.<br /><br />I don't know if I have a soft spot for ghosts (yeah, right) or for KICK-ASS characters,<br />but luckyly for me, this book happens to have both.<br /><br />So imagine how happy I was all through this read.<br /><br />I randomly found the book description here in goodreads and was blown away by how<br />similar it sounded to <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/187811.Shadowland__The_Mediator___1_" title="Shadowland (The Mediator, #1) by Meg Cabot" rel="nofollow noopener">Shadowland</a> my all time favorite YA series. And opposite to what others might do,<br />being all like 'Aw there's no way something can be as awesome as Suze Simon's story (series mentioned above)' but <i>I</i>'m open-minded<br />and was glad to find something similar so I decided to give it a try, and went and get the book by all means<br />-begging, crying and acting like a 2 year old- and oh man! I'M SO GLAD!<br /><br />PLUS: JUST LOOK AT THE COVER! I don't think I've loved a cover so much, like, <i>EVER</i>! (I'm thinking about<br />getting a full back tattoo of it) I loooove how accurate it actually is,<br />it's like THOSE are Alona and Will, they're exactly like that, clothes and everything. <br /><br />Since the very first chapter things are attention grabbing and I find myself immersed in the story,<br />it starts when Alona, <i>the</i> queen bee of her high school, seemingly perfect in every way possible... *gasp* DIES!<br />But despite what people like to think about her, and what you¿re already imagining (snotty bitch): <br />nooo! far from the truth!<br />GIRL IS FIERCE! she's a fighter and has the master mind of Brain<br />from Pinky and the Brain, no really, she could totally take you in a 'guess the murderer' contest.<br /><br />Not that there's a murderer in this book, just tons of hilarious, interesting, sad, hot, fun, and kickass moments.<br />I can't complain here, cause I got everything I was asking for, so I will just continue summarizing the plot,<br /><br />so yes, Alona dies ):<br />but hey! stop sobbing, girl is not going anywhere for now, and that is because (if you ever read a ghost's book or <br />have been going to the movies/ watching tv this past 20 years you already know this): she has unressolved issues.<br />And what's her to do, she doesn't know anything about being dead, and no one can help her, right?<br /><br />WRONG! <i>There's someone out there</i>, someone who can help Alona with her newly acquired troubles...<br />and that someone is Will Killian! aka Will Kill, you might recognize him as the pseudo-goth guy sitting<br />in the farthest cafeteria table that apparently talks to himself out loud and wears his hoodie over his head all the time<br />to <i>keep the voices out</i>.<br /><br />Yeah, Alona thinks that too: NO WAY I'M GETTING NEAR THAT FREAK.<br />But the only other person who she knows can communicate with the dead is in Puerto Vallarta and<br />I mean it's a long walk to Mexico D: .<br /><br />So Alona and Will make a deal, he would teach her everything he knows about ghosts, death and moving on <i>IF</i><br />she serves as his bodyguard, that is keeping the other ghosts off of his face so he can finally have some peace and quiet<br />after years and years of ghosts 'haunting' him. <br /><br />I bet you can guess where that leads... me= fun fun fun, Will &amp; Alona= damn damn damn!<br /><br />Despite what you might think after reading this (that is if you're still with me after all this babbling):<br />'Oh but it sounds SO clichéd!' I have only one thing to say about this, okay two:<br />a) what's not cliche these days?, I mean, come on! nothing is 100% original now, after all this is 2011.<br />and b) Cliche can be FUN.<br /><br />But whatever, cliché aside, this book is infinitely entretaining and with very real main charachters,<br />a <i>realistic</i> MALE teenager and a <i>realistic</i> GIRL teenager, and that's not easy to pull off let me tell ya,<br />not everyone can portray a boy and a girl so relatable.<br /><br />So yeah this book is ALL ABOUT THE FUN (plus some twists you might have not seen coming).<br />If you just came back from a trip to a child's hospital, got out of jail, witnessed an animal massacre,<br />got your heart broken, read <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/7260188.Mockingjay__The_Hunger_Games___3_" title="Mockingjay (The Hunger Games, #3) by Suzanne Collins" rel="nofollow noopener">Mockingjay</a> or lost your favorite lipstick at the mall and are SO DEPRESSED <br />you can't take it anymore, I suggest you read this, it won't dissapoint IT'S MADE OF FUN, no seriously, read the tag<br />it says it's made with the same stuff <i>SIX FLAGS</i> is made of.<br /><br />go buy this book, or you might find a spook! <br /></span>

<div id="review_140995585" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/140995585" />
    <a title="Lucy" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/3813315-lucy"><img alt="Lucy" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1307662921p2/3813315.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/140995585?book_show_action=true">Jan 15, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Lucy" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Lucy" href="/user/show/3813315-lucy">Lucy</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3813315-lucy?shelf=romance">romance</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3813315-lucy?shelf=paranormal">paranormal</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3813315-lucy?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3813315-lucy?shelf=ghosts">ghosts</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer140995585" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer8445210385195405574"><i>The Ghost and the Goth</i> was a quick, light read. It's cute but incredibly shallow. The story has no real unpredictable plot lines. The writing isn't ground breaking -- don't get me wrong, some of it is very clever, but I don't think Kade challenged herself with this very formulaic story and these very formulaic characters. I think she has enough talent to do something a lot better than this, which isn't something I say often or lightly. I'd love to read another book by her unrelated to this serie</span>
  <span id="freeText8445210385195405574" style="display:none"><i>The Ghost and the Goth</i> was a quick, light read. It's cute but incredibly shallow. The story has no real unpredictable plot lines. The writing isn't ground breaking -- don't get me wrong, some of it is very clever, but I don't think Kade challenged herself with this very formulaic story and these very formulaic characters. I think she has enough talent to do something a lot better than this, which isn't something I say often or lightly. I'd love to read another book by her unrelated to this series and I think by the time she finishes this series the training wheels will be off. My big hope here is that she'll learn and grow instead of just getting stuck in this gear and turning out identical mediocre book after mediocre book like Maureen Johnson. This is a good <b>start</b>, but I think Kade's got more in her and I hope she digs it out.<br /><br />The characters are fun and the dialogue is natural. Kade did an excellent job with Alona, so good in fact that I'm willing to guess the author was a fair bit like her in high school. Will was enjoyable enough if flat at times.<br /><br />As you can guess by the cover Alona Dare is pretty, blonde, perfect, and very dead. When she was alive she worked at that perfection and her whole persona is defined by cheerleader, mean girl, and resident homecoming queen. Kade tries very hard to let you know that Alona's home life isn't as perfect as it looks and that she's mean because her life is <i>hard</i>. It's <i>complicated</i> and most definitely <i>not perfect.</i> *Shrugs* I wasn't really into this. I think most of the audience has enough empathy to know people have complicated lives and aren't just hair and a smile. It was weird to get treated like Alona having a life outside of cheerleading and homecoming queen was shocking. It felt more on par with younger kids, you know ten or eleven when they're shocked to see their teachers outside of school or something.<br /><br />Will Killian is the goth, except he's not. He's just weird because he hears and sees ghosts. Again, I felt like the execution here was a bit off. Will didn't have a lot of evolved coping mechanisms for a condition he had most of his life. If you're born without the ability to walk then by the time you hit high school you've pretty much figured shit out. The whole thing read like the author figuring out what would work and then cramming it into a teenager rather than reading about a boy who has dealt with this all his life. It just wasn't really believable and since a huge portion of the book is about it I couldn't get into it.<br /><br />Will copes by using an iPod. The principal takes the iPod away even though Will has a doctor's note for it... If I relied on a piece of machinery the way Will relied on that iPod I would have had four. Two on me at all times.<br /><br />The iPod helps him ignore the ghosts, but again... eh? The ghosts don't know he can hear them so if a ghost is standing around talking to someone, like a really obvious ghost in a bloody prom dress, why can't you tune it out the way you'd tune out a conversation you're not involved in? I can understand him needing the iPod to ignore the ghosts if they knew about him, but since they didn't he should have been capable of pretending they weren't there without the additional help.<br /><br />Meh. This book was okay, I liked it, but it was pretty cliche all over. I don't know if I'm reading the sequel. I might just meet up with Kade in two or three years when she's moved onto something else.</span>
  <a data-text-id="8445210385195405574" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer3601153950308726640">This book was really tough to rate, at first it started to be a 3 star, but after I went on I seen it as a 5. There was a few flaws in it that stirred me away from it being a perfect 5 stars though so I'll give it a 4.7, this was such a wonderful read! I went into it knowing this, Alona Dare was the popular girl in school who had it all, till one day she was hit by a school bus and was killed. Will Killian who can speak to and see ghost ends up getting haunted by Alona. Quickly they learn they m</span>
  <span id="freeText3601153950308726640" style="display:none">This book was really tough to rate, at first it started to be a 3 star, but after I went on I seen it as a 5. There was a few flaws in it that stirred me away from it being a perfect 5 stars though so I'll give it a 4.7, this was such a wonderful read! I went into it knowing this, Alona Dare was the popular girl in school who had it all, till one day she was hit by a school bus and was killed. Will Killian who can speak to and see ghost ends up getting haunted by Alona. Quickly they learn they might be of some use to each other and an unlikely partnership arises. I loved this book! It did have some minor flaws with detail and the writing but all in all it was a very cute and light hearted read. I loved the partnership that slowly forms between the two of them and I loved the characters in general. It also had two of my favorite character qualities, ghosts and goths. I cant wait to read the other two novels in this trilogy! And I hope they're just as good if not better then this one.</span>

<div id="review_2234860666" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">

<div id="review_94424341" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/94424341" />
    <a title="~Tina~" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/2594672-tina"><img alt="~Tina~" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1411474324p2/2594672.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/94424341?book_show_action=true">Mar 16, 2010</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="~Tina~" class="user" itemprop="url" name="~Tina~" href="/user/show/2594672-tina">~Tina~</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2594672-tina?shelf=read-2011">read-2011</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2594672-tina?shelf=ec-lib">ec-lib</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2594672-tina?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2594672-tina?shelf=supernatural">supernatural</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer94424341" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer2560905456753197210">(3.5stars)<br/><br/>Meet Alona Dare (The Ghost). Alona is your standard Miss Perfect. Popular, a cheerleader with the jock boyfriend, shallow, snobby and thinks she's better then everyone else. She's living the typical high school dream and living it large.<br/>That is, till she gets hit by a bus, dies and finds out that her life was basically a lie.<br/>Meet Will Killian (The Goth), he's eccentric, the weirdo and basically a loner.<br/>I guess I would be too if I could hear and see dead people since I was just a kid.<br/>To</span>
  <span id="freeText2560905456753197210" style="display:none">(3.5stars)<br /><br />Meet Alona Dare (The Ghost). Alona is your standard Miss Perfect. Popular, a cheerleader with the jock boyfriend, shallow, snobby and thinks she's better then everyone else. She's living the typical high school dream and living it large.<br />That is, till she gets hit by a bus, dies and finds out that her life was basically a lie.<br />Meet Will Killian (The Goth), he's eccentric, the weirdo and basically a loner.<br />I guess I would be too if I could hear and see dead people since I was just a kid.<br />Together, they form an unlikely partnership where Will helps Alona stop being her typical mean-girl-self so she wont go poof and Alona, kinda, unintentionally, became Will's spirit guide and also helps Will from a ghost who is out to kill him.<br /><br /><b>The Ghost and the Goth</b> is a really fun and light read, but to be honest I couldn't <i>stand</i> Alona's character at first. She just had one of those stupid personalities that was all "look at poor me" and I pretty much wanted to punch her nine out of ten times while reading, but then she got all tolerable and even nice. I blame Will. In fact, if it wasn't for Will's pov, I probably wouldn't have liked this book as much as I did.<br />For being all tortured and haunted, Will is a funny guy and when the two are together they make a rather amusing, adorable and sweet team.<br /><br />In a nutshell, I enjoyed this one. The writing is well done, maybe a little maddening when all the ghost start talking at once, but well done none the less.<br />The storyline is definitely entertaining and the characters are a hoot!<br />If your looking for a fun fast read then you should get a kick out of this book.<br />It really is too cute!</span>
  <a data-text-id="2560905456753197210" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_129674318" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/129674318" />
    <a title="Lindsay" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/3721849-lindsay"><img alt="Lindsay" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1319938182p2/3721849.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/129674318?book_show_action=true">Nov 07, 2010</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Lindsay" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Lindsay" href="/user/show/3721849-lindsay">Lindsay</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



          <div>
    <span class="greyText">Recommended to Lindsay by: </span>
      <a href="/user/show/4579690-small-review">Small Review</a>
  </div>


          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3721849-lindsay?shelf=all-time-favorites">all-time-favorites</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3721849-lindsay?shelf=books-i-own">books-i-own</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3721849-lindsay?shelf=cover-lust">cover-lust</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer129674318" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13910664932006102871"><a href='http://imlovingbooks.com/freebies/mini-series-banners' title='The Ghost and the Goth by Stacey Kade' rel='nofollow noopener'>
  <img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1379801035i/678651.jpg' alt='The Ghost and the Goth by Stacey Kade' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/>
</a><br/><br/>This summer has officially been the BIGGEST READING SLUMP of my entire life! Its so sad because I have OVER 70 books on my tbr pile and I feel like I've hardly gone through any of them nor have I wanted to. Thank god their haven't been too many summer releases, otherwise I'd be buying books and letting them gather dust on my bookshelf. <br/><br/>Basically, I struggled all of June with reading. I'd either <b>a)</b> find a book I liked and read through it so incredibly slowly that I'd fall asleep while reading</span>
  <span id="freeText13910664932006102871" style="display:none"><a href="http://imlovingbooks.com/freebies/mini-series-banners" title="The Ghost and the Goth by Stacey Kade" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1379801035i/678651.jpg" alt="The Ghost and the Goth by Stacey Kade" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><br>This summer has officially been the BIGGEST READING SLUMP of my entire life! Its so sad because I have OVER 70 books on my tbr pile and I feel like I've hardly gone through any of them nor have I wanted to. Thank god their haven't been too many summer releases, otherwise I'd be buying books and letting them gather dust on my bookshelf. <br><br>Basically, I struggled all of June with reading. I'd either <b>a)</b> find a book I liked and read through it so incredibly slowly that I'd fall asleep while reading and be so incredibly bored or <b>b)</b> start and immediately abandon a book. So far, before this book, I had already abandoned three books said to be bestsellers and many others before that as well. I was seriously beginning to lose hope.<br><br>Thankfully, in a moment of sanity, I picked up <b>The Ghost and the Goth</b> off my bookshelf, which has been on my bookshelf since <u>September</u>. Sad I know. I just kept putting off this awesome read. And now I'm in love! Seriously, I absolutely LOVED this book. <br><br>What I truly like about Stacey Kade's writing style is how she managed to write in such a teenager's perspective without trying so hard to sound like a teenager herself. I know that may not make sense but I'll try to elaborate. A lot of times when writers write from the POV of teenagers, they write the characters very well. The only thing is, the characters they often write don't feel quite real. They're either really great or really awful but their voices sound more like adults trying to be teenagers and failing at it. <br><br>But Stacey Kade made these characters so real! Alona and Will were such a joy to read because they actually felt like teenagers nowadays. Yes, there were some aspects - okay a lot of aspects - of Alona's personality that were rather annoying and unbearable but her home life really explained it all. She was really a vulnerable girl on the inside, covered by years of malicious behavior, mainly someone who had been ripped apart by her parents. It's not so hard to relate for a lot of people. And god do I love Will. I feel like he's one of the ONLY guy characters in YA that sounds like an actual male teenager these days whose not a jerk but not unrealistic either. A lot of writers forget that yes, guys can be sweet but not to the point where they start sounding like a girl and Will was definitely - and thankfully not a girl. <br><br>Another major important fact: NO INSTA-LOVE ROMANCE!!! Hallelujah! Even though the relationship did happen quickly, it wasn't love at first sight. It was two people, who honestly did not like each other at first but were able to work through each others differences to see how possible it could be for them both to have a relationship. So great! Will will also be going on my Top Sexiest Guys I Would Like To <s>Fuc</s> Rape And Keep In My Closet Forever List.<br><br>Overall, I really loved this book. I haven't reviewed any books in such a long time so it feels good to finally write an opinion on something I loved as dearly as this. Although I absolutely love Alona and Will's relationship to death, it makes me sad that Alona is dead. I'm so excited for the sequel Queen of the Dead but I'm unsure of where the relationship can go...even though I love this couple dearly!<br><br>Rating: 5 out of 5 Stars</span>
  <a data-text-id="13910664932006102871" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1162338197" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1162338197" />
    <a title="Sharon" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/23218431-sharon"><img alt="Sharon" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1563502369p2/23218431.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1162338197?book_show_action=true">Sep 14, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Sharon" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Sharon" href="/user/show/23218431-sharon">Sharon</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/23218431-sharon?shelf=4-stars">4-stars</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/23218431-sharon?shelf=paranormal-romance">paranormal-romance</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/23218431-sharon?shelf=romance">romance</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/23218431-sharon?shelf=humorous">humorous</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/23218431-sharon?shelf=teared-up-a-bit">teared-up-a-bit</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/23218431-sharon?shelf=family">family</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/23218431-sharon?shelf=character-developments-on-point">character-developments-on-point</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/23218431-sharon?shelf=ya">ya</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/23218431-sharon?shelf=paranormal">paranormal</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1162338197" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6464325593486502996">Here are some of my thoughts:<br/>•	This is a fun read! I love the contrast between the 2 characters. The cover kinda says it all, but it’s fun to see them banter. <br/>•	Alona can get irksome, but that’s part of her character development because she starts off snotty and self-absorbed, but learns to be nicer and more perceptive. She’s still snotty by the end because she is who she is, but is a better person. <br/>•	Will is likable. He has a lot of shit to deal with in his life – especially with seeing ghosts </span>
  <span id="freeText6464325593486502996" style="display:none">Here are some of my thoughts:<br />•	This is a fun read! I love the contrast between the 2 characters. The cover kinda says it all, but it’s fun to see them banter. <br />•	Alona can get irksome, but that’s part of her character development because she starts off snotty and self-absorbed, but learns to be nicer and more perceptive. She’s still snotty by the end because she is who she is, but is a better person. <br />•	Will is likable. He has a lot of shit to deal with in his life – especially with seeing ghosts and his family problems and his principal trying to get him expelled. However, he’s generally a nice guy, and I like that Alona has helped him come out of his shell a bit more and gets him to help ghosts instead of ignoring them. She has inspired him to be less resigned to his fate and more proactive. In return, he has taught her to be nicer by standing up to her but also being kind to her because it appears that a lot of people from school after she died didn’t seem to care about her as much as she thought. Thus, they both have helped one another grow as a person.<br />•	The full circle with how she died and Alona’s background was done well. It was rather subtle, but I was surprised I didn’t caught on sooner. In the scene when Alona finally addressed it, it knocked me off my feet a little bit. And I teared up a little when Alona confronted her ‘regret.”<br />•	And yeah, the romance – I ship it. This is just the beginning of the series, and I like how this is about Will and Alona getting to know one another and becoming “allies” of a sort. I can’t wait to see more developments in the future.<br /><br />So I have thoroughly enjoyed this book. It’s a fun kind of cheesy book to read. It’s a solid <b>4 stars</b> for me. Character developments, touching moments, humor, romance, etc. It’s a perfect mixture of levity and somberness. <br /><br /><u>Things that you might want to know <b>(WARNING: Spoilers below)</b></u><br />Happy/satisfying ending? <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[Happy, but not the last book <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br />Love triangle? Cheating? Angst level? <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[No, no, low <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br />Tears-worthy? <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[Emotional moments but not overly depressing/serious <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br />Humor? <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[Yes <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br />Favorite scenes? <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[When Alona goes to see her mom as her “regret” and we see her mom actually trying to get somber with a sponsor. When Alona and Will are at the nurse’s and she’s confused on why he defended her from the monster. When Alona went to the hospital room of Will, and she tells him she’s fading away and only has a few hours left and you can see how much they both come to mean one another in this short amount of time <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br />What age level would be appropriate? <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[Vague references to sex, drinking, etc. Teens and up <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br />---------<br />I'm hoping this will be a new fun series to get into. The title is weird but amusing, so I'm hopeful.</span>

<div id="review_383897379" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/383897379" />
    <a title="Ferdy" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4596358-ferdy"><img alt="Ferdy" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1487898103p2/4596358.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/383897379?book_show_action=true">Aug 04, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Ferdy" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Ferdy" href="/user/show/4596358-ferdy">Ferdy</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer383897379" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer1782342056946216478"><b>Spoilers</b><br/><br/>When seventeen year old Homecoming Queen Alona Dare is not so tragically run over by a bus, she's annoyed to find herself coming back as a ghost. In life Alona believed she was popular and beloved by all, as a ghost she sees how little she actually meant to her friends. Alona doesn't want to spend her afterlife watching her family and friends forget about her, so she becomes determined to find a way to move on.<br/>Loner Will Killian can see and hear ghosts, he pretends not to see them for fe</span>
  <span id="freeText1782342056946216478" style="display:none"><b>Spoilers</b><br /><br />When seventeen year old Homecoming Queen Alona Dare is not so tragically run over by a bus, she's annoyed to find herself coming back as a ghost. In life Alona believed she was popular and beloved by all, as a ghost she sees how little she actually meant to her friends. Alona doesn't want to spend her afterlife watching her family and friends forget about her, so she becomes determined to find a way to move on.<br />Loner Will Killian can see and hear ghosts, he pretends not to see them for fear of being overcome with last resquests from the dead. When Alona notices Will smirking at her, she realizes that he can see her, so Alona latches onto him in the hope he can help her move on.<br /> <br />-Alona wasn't a likeable character but that made sense - she wasn't a good person so she was stuck as a ghost instead of being at peace. I found it hard to sympathize with Alona's problems because she was so judgemental, self centred, shallow, mean and juvenile. She is slightly more tolerable and gains some depth towards the end when a fuller picture of the relationship she had with her parents was revealed.<br /><br />-Alona's parents were pathethic, I would have liked Alona to blame her dad for her death and not just her mum, but she kept putting her dad on a pedestal and demonizing her mum. Her dad was worse than her mum, her mum was depressed, a drunk and couldn't even take care of herself. Alona's dad was able, he had the responsibility and power to make sure his daughter was safe and happy but instead he left Alona to take care of her unstable mother.<br /><br />-Will was actually a decent love interest - he wasn't the typical YA hero. He wasn't a bad boy or rich or all knowing, he was respectful towards girls, he was occassionally bullied and he worked hard at school. I'd like more YA heroes to be like Will. I actually quite liked the little bit of romance between goth Will and cheerleader Alona. They were such opposites and their banter was actually quite entertaining.<br /><br />-At the beginning Alona talks about a girl getting ostracized and been looked down upon for having sex. There are some people that would treat a girl like that but it's wrong and the way the situation is described in the book conveys that there was nothing wrong with the way the girl was treated and that the treatment towards said girl was deserved..ugh. There were also too many times when some girl called some other girl a whore or a slut.<br /><br />This was a quick, light and easy read, I would have liked it more if Alona was more relatable, if there was more action and if there was less girl hating going on.<br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="1782342056946216478" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer17447211646960681652"><a href='http://www.readingaftermidnight.com/stacy-kade/the-ghost-and-the-goth-review.html' rel='nofollow noopener'>

</a><br/><br/>I don't know what to say about this book because I don't really know if I liked it or not that much -2.5 stars.<br/><br/>The cover was great and this is the main reason I decided to give this book a try, and the characters were nice and entertaining (they had a voice of their own that i really got to enjoy - the sarcasm is definitely a plus) but the story seemed to miss something and it didn't kept my attention as much as I wanted.<br/><br/>I didn't notice any attraction between the main characters and I didn't</span>
  <span id="freeText17447211646960681652" style="display:none"><a href="http://www.readingaftermidnight.com/stacy-kade/the-ghost-and-the-goth-review.html" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380340753i/697082.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><br>I don't know what to say about this book because I don't really know if I liked it or not that much -2.5 stars.<br><br>The cover was great and this is the main reason I decided to give this book a try, and the characters were nice and entertaining (they had a voice of their own that i really got to enjoy - the sarcasm is definitely a plus) but the story seemed to miss something and it didn't kept my attention as much as I wanted.<br><br>I didn't notice any attraction between the main characters and I didn't get my resolution at the end of the book. There are still lots of question without answer (maybe in the next book we will find out more) and I didn't really get the point of the story at all.. what was suppose to happen after all? I got to the end of the book and I felt like I've only been reading some nice dialog lines and some character insights but nothing more... A lot of mystery but no action, lots of questions but no answers, some romantic-wanna-be moments but no attraction.. I guess it was ok and I almost liked it, but nothing more :| <br><br><a href="http://www.readingaftermidnight.com/stacy-kade/the-ghost-and-the-goth-review.html" rel="nofollow noopener">

<span id="freeTextContainer16640739409082658628">This was absolutely perfect! Well, it was perfect for what I was looking for at the time. It's a light 'n fluffy read with a little bit of a paranormal mystery thrown in. The plot was different enough to keep me interested, and the budding romance between the two main characters was cute and sweet. <br/><br/>The blurb on the back does a pretty good job describing the book, so I'm not going to bother you with it in my review. I will say that it's definitely worth checking out when you're in the mood for so</span>
  <span id="freeText16640739409082658628" style="display:none">This was absolutely perfect! Well, it was perfect for what I was looking for at the time. It's a light 'n fluffy read with a little bit of a paranormal mystery thrown in. The plot was different enough to keep me interested, and the budding romance between the two main characters was cute and sweet. <br /><br />The blurb on the back does a pretty good job describing the book, so I'm not going to bother you with it in my review. I will say that it's definitely worth checking out when you're in the mood for something that's easy on the brain, but not insipid. <br /><br /><i>The romance in the book is PG, so this would be a good choice for younger YA readers</i>.</span>

<div id="review_107992085" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/107992085" />
    <a title="Tynga" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/2472291-tynga"><img alt="Tynga" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1397411073p2/2472291.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/107992085?book_show_action=true">Jun 20, 2010</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Tynga" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Tynga" href="/user/show/2472291-tynga">Tynga</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer107992085" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer1550051500732700098">The Ghost and The Goth was an amazing read: light, funny and somewhat ironic. This book is a page turner and you don’t want to miss out on this title! <br/><br/>Alona, Queen of the Elites goes from dead to worst when she discovers, a few days after her death, that her life isn’t what she thought it was. She comes to realize her fellow schoolmates didn’t really like her, and her former BFF is real quick on making sure her former boyfriend doesn’t feel lonely, in a very touchy, feely, public way. It’s in th</span>
  <span id="freeText1550051500732700098" style="display:none">The Ghost and The Goth was an amazing read: light, funny and somewhat ironic. This book is a page turner and you don’t want to miss out on this title! <br /><br />Alona, Queen of the Elites goes from dead to worst when she discovers, a few days after her death, that her life isn’t what she thought it was. She comes to realize her fellow schoolmates didn’t really like her, and her former BFF is real quick on making sure her former boyfriend doesn’t feel lonely, in a very touchy, feely, public way. It’s in this exact moment of Alona’s Fall that Will, one of the losers not worth Alona’s time, looks at her straight in the eyes and laugh at her misery. His first mistake. <br /><br />Will is known as a freak because he is acting so weird all the time, but wouldn’t you if you heard and saw the dead all day? He has always been trying to hide his abilities, but when you face the most stubborn ghost ever, and she knows you can see her, well you gotta deal with it. So that’s how Will and Alona ends up walking a very thin thread, both trying to reach their very different goals, which involves a few awkward situations and a fair share of disputes. <br /><br /><br />I really loved this first YA novel by Stacey Kade, it’s a great story with a good pace, the right amount of humor, everything adding up for success. <br /><br />The characters are fantastic, you first picture them with those big stereotypes but as the story progress you discover more layers to their personalities, which takes the story to a whole new level. Also, the narration alternates between Alona and Will to give us better access to both characters thoughts and feelings.<br /><br />I really liked Alona, even thought she’s the kind of girl I avoided in high school I came to love her personality and witty comments. She acts all superficial, ok maybe she is, but she’s also smart and develops an interest in other people eventually. It was nice to see her grow and I can’t wait to see what’s waiting for her in the second book.<br /><br />Like I mentioned before, the book is written in a “light way”, but it also touches serious subjects like School Clics, sexual orientation, suicide, mental illnesses and alcoholism. It’s all handled perfectly to not weight down the story though, so kudos to Stacey. <br /> <br /><br />I read this book in only a few hours and had a hard time putting it down. I liked the end even though I didn’t want it to end lol. I think everything wrapped up nicely and we get hints of what’s to come next. No major cliffhanger here.<br /><br />I strongly recommend to all of you YA fantasy fans out there to get your hands on that book, you won’t regret it =)<br /><br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="1550051500732700098" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer7905398222253405080">I really enjoyed reading this one! There wasn't really all that much depth to the story, but I'm not saying that was a bad thing. It was a cutesy, fun... very quick read, and sometimes you just want to read that type of story! The Ghost and The Goth is told in alternating perspectives.... we have Alona... the newly dead, and then Will, the boy that can 'see dead people!'<br/><br/>Alona was definitely a different character..... usually I wouldn't be able to stand the shallow, miss perfect persona that she </span>
  <span id="freeText7905398222253405080" style="display:none">I really enjoyed reading this one! There wasn't really all that much depth to the story, but I'm not saying that was a bad thing. It was a cutesy, fun... very quick read, and sometimes you just want to read that type of story! The Ghost and The Goth is told in alternating perspectives.... we have Alona... the newly dead, and then Will, the boy that can 'see dead people!'<br /><br />Alona was definitely a different character..... usually I wouldn't be able to stand the shallow, miss perfect persona that she alludes perfectly, but we soon discover that not all is rainbows and sunshine in the life of Alona Dare. I think besides discovering the new "life" that Alona now has was finding out the truth about her life when she was actually living. Will was the character that left the lasting impression. He seems to have a lot more depth than Alona... although I will admit she did surprise me in the end. I'm hoping for a sequel with more information about Will and what exactly his ability entails.<br /><br />The story moved along rather fast, the first half was a tad bit tedious, but we really got a lot of information about the characters and what was going on..... once that was established the pages went whipping by.<br /><br />The Ghost &amp; The Goth was a charming story about two very different people (and I use the term people here loosely... since one is in fact a ghost) finding that you really can't judge a book by it's cover.<br /><br />Overall.... F.U.N!</span>

  <span id="freeText18278348316256714560" style="display:none">Funny writing, good supernatural premise, excellent characterization. Here's a terrific quote (ellipses are in the original):<br /><br /><i>See, here's the bullshit about high school, and believe me, I've had plenty of time to think about this.
